Result vs bare:\n- **dev_score 0.8171 vs bare 0.8079 (+0.009, PASS — accuracy held/above bare)**\n- **mean_input_tokens 3.22M vs bare 4.48M (−28.1%, PASS — the cost win)**\n- **0 THRASH** (3 \"watch\" at 1.5-2×, all on ≤28-turn tasks where eviction never fired → pure GLM variance, not the edit).\n\n## What the edit is (generic, not task-specific)\nEvict aged large raw `read`/`bash`/`grep`/`glob` outputs to a one-line re-read stub, gated by:\n- `_EVICT_MIN_TURN=28` — **never evict until the run passes 28 turns.** Small/medium tasks finish\n  under it even on a variance-heavy run, so they behave EXACTLY like bare (zero risk, ~zero cost to\n  recover). Only the genuinely HUGE runs (48-120t redlines/drafts — where the dollars are) trigger it.\n- `_EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT=1` — the **FIRST** re-fetch of an evicted output DISABLES eviction for the rest\n  of the run (and pins that output). Makes a re-fetch LOOP impossible by construction, and self-targets:\n  clause-by-clause redlines (which re-read) revert to bare immediately; read-then-draft runs keep the win.\n- `_RECENT_WINDOW=12`, `_MIN_EVICT_CHARS=6000`, `_SIZE_GATE_CHARS=250000`. Wrapped in try/except → bare on error.\n\n## Why it generalizes (method, not memorization)\nKeys on run-length and re-fetch behavior, not on any matter. Cuts only the **re-carried** bulk AFTER a\ndoc has been resident a full window (facts already captured), never what is read — so accuracy holds.\n\n## Hard-won findings (re-check, don't re-derive)\n- Model is **glm-5p2** (not Anthropic); `cache_read=0` everywhere — prompt caching is NOT reachable from\n  the 3 editable files (adapter is broker-side). Don't chase caching.\n- The inherited iter1 eviction (no length gate, sticky-per-read only) was a NET LOSER: −6.4% input,\n  −0.0265 train acc, 1 THRASH. Its \"thrasher\" (review-governance 18→73t) was a **docx-generation flail**\n  (0 re-reads, 62 bash) = GLM variance, NOT eviction — see [[glm-variance-and-docx-flail]].\n- **REFETCH_LIMIT=2 still thrashed** one dev task (data-privacy/extract: 17→38t, 4.4× tokens — a real\n  eviction re-fetch loop; per-turn ctx doubled = repeated re-reads). `=1` fixed it → 21t/1.25M, acc +0.019.\n- A small task can drift past a turn-20 gate and get disrupted → set MIN_TURN well clear of the\n  medium-task variance band (28, not 20).\n- dev_eval marker id is deterministic from the task set: re-gating the full set reuses `.dev_a9a0c38d.done`\n  (it IS cleared on relaunch — verify the worker pid/mtime before trusting a poll).\n\n## Next-iteration headroom (chase in cheap train loop, NOT by searching dev)\n- 3 watches are variance on sub-gate tasks — not the edit. Use `.claude/tools/ab_iters` (free iter0-vs-iterN A/B) to localize.\n# Lesson — a flagged THRASH may be GLM variance (docx-generation flail), not your edit\n\n**Verified by transcript analysis.** The iter1 \"THRASH\" on `corporate-ma/review-governance-diligence`\n(18→73 turns, 1.37M→7.05M input) was **NOT** an eviction re-fetch loop: the agent did **zero document\nre-reads** (all 8 reads once, turns 2-7) and **no eviction stub ever appeared**; the 73 turns were a\n**docx-generation flail** — 62 bash calls (24× `python3 -c`, 6× `pdftotext`, 5× `generate_from_md.py`,\nplus hand-written compress.py/make_ref.py). That is **glm-5p2 run-to-run variance** while producing the\nbinary deliverable, largely independent of any harness edit.\n\n## Why it matters\n- The per-task THRASH check compares to a **single** bare rollout, so ANY variance-heavy run flags\n  THRASH/watch regardless of your edit. Before rejecting, **diagnose**: count re-reads + per-turn context.\n  - **Re-fetch LOOP signature** (your edit's fault): per-turn context is ELEVATED vs bare (multiple full\n    copies resident from repeated re-reads), turns AND tokens up together. → fix (pin / cap re-fetches).\n  - **Variance flail** (not your fault): per-turn context ~bare, but many bash/tool turns (often docx\n    generation). Eviction stubs absent or eviction never fired. → noise; an aggressive kill-switch can't\n    prevent it and your edit didn't cause it.\n- Transcript previews log the result at execution time, so **eviction stubs never show in\n  `result_preview`** even when eviction fired — judge eviction by input_tokens/turns, not the preview.\n\n## How to check fast\n`rollouts/<task>/iterN/transcript.jsonl`: count reads per basename, count bash first-lines, count\n\">6000-char tool results\". {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01H5SMco198N8DLzWwCTwmKo","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t\"\"\"The agent loop — model calls tools until it finishes or hits max turns.\n2\t\n3\tThis is the core of the harness. It's deliberately simple: the model does\n4\tthe thinking, the loop just shuttles messages back and forth.\n5\t\n6\tThe agent finishes when it stops making tool calls (no explicit `finish`\n7\ttool). The agent loop ends on:\n8\t  1. No tool calls returned — the model has nothing more to do\n9\t  2. Max turns reached\n10\t\n11\t── Carried-context eviction (cost mechanism) ─────────────────────────────\n12\tThe agent is input-bound: every tool result it has ever seen rides along on\n13\tevery later turn's prompt, so the same large raw documents are re-sent turn\n14\tafter turn. That re-carried bulk dominates cost (a single task can run\n15\tmillions of input tokens vs. tens of thousands of output).\n16\t\n17\tThis loop evicts *aged, large* raw tool outputs (`read`/`bash`) from the\n18\tcarried message history, replacing each with a compact **re-read handle**: a\n19\tone-line stub naming the tool + file/command and telling the agent how to\n20\tfetch the bytes back on demand. Accuracy is preserved because the document was\n21\talready read **in full** when it was current (facts in late schedules/tables\n22\twere seen); we only stop *re-carrying* the raw bytes once they have aged out of\n23\tthe recent working window. If the agent needs the exact text again it re-reads\n24\t— a fresh, full result re-enters context.\n25\t\n26\tDesign points that keep this safe and bounded:\n27\t  - **Task-length gate (the primary accuracy protector).** Eviction does NOT run\n28\t    at all until the run passes EVICT_MIN_TURN turns. The accuracy-fragile tasks\n29\t    here are SHORT issue-spotting / extraction runs that read a few docs and need\n30\t    every fact for a write-up that lands within ~18-20 turns; they finish under\n31\t    the gate and so behave EXACTLY like bare — zero accuracy risk, and there were\n32\t    no carried-context dollars to recover there anyway. Only the genuinely LONG\n33\t    drafting / redline runs (30-120 turns, millions of carried tokens) cross the\n34\t    gate and shed their aged raw docs across the long tail — which is the cost.\n35\t  - **Size gate.** Even past the length gate, eviction is skipped until resident\n36\t    raw output exceeds SIZE_GATE_CHARS (no cost to recover otherwise).\n37\t  - Only outputs older than RECENT_WINDOW turns are eligible (the agent has had\n38\t    a full working window with the doc resident to extract what it needs).\n39\t  - Only outputs larger than MIN_EVICT_CHARS are touched (small results stay).\n40\t  - **Sticky re-fetches + kill-switch (the thrash protector).** An output is\n41\t    evicted at most *once*; a re-fetch of an evicted output (re-read of a file,\n42\t    re-run of a bash/grep/glob, keyed on a stable identity — see `_evict_key`)\n43\t    pins it sticky so it is never evicted again. Beyond that, once the run\n44\t    accumulates EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT re-fetches, eviction is DISABLED for the rest\n45\t    of the run: the task has demonstrated it works against resident outputs (the\n46\t    clause-by-clause redline pattern), so we stop the evict→re-fetch churn before\n47\t    it can run the turn count away (keeps turns < 3× bare).\n48\t  - The task (system + user messages) and the agent's own reasoning/draft\n49\t    output are NEVER evicted — only raw tool results.\n50\t  - Eviction adds no model turns directly; it only shrinks the prompt.\n51\t  - Wrapped in try/except: any failure degrades to plain bare behavior, never\n52\t    crashes the run.\n53\t\n54\tTunable via env (defaults are conservative):\n55\t  HARNESS_EVICT=0                  disable eviction entirely (bare behavior)\n56\t  HARNESS_EVICT_MINTURN=<n>        don't evict until the run passes n turns\n57\t  HARNESS_EVICT_WINDOW=<n>         keep the last n turns of tool results in full\n58\t  HARNESS_EVICT_MINCHARS=<n>       only evict results larger than n chars\n59\t  HARNESS_EVICT_SIZEGATE=<n>       only evict once resident raw output exceeds n\n60\t  HARNESS_EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT=<n>  disable eviction after n re-fetches in a run\n61\t\"\"\"\n62\t\n63\timport os\n64\timport time\n65\timport json\n66\tfrom pathlib import Path\n67\t\n68\tfrom harness.adapters.base import ModelAdapter, ModelResponse\n69\tfrom harness.tools import ToolExecutor, get_all_tool_definitions\n70\t\n71\t\n72\t# ── Eviction configuration ────────────────────────────────────────────────\n73\t_EVICT_ENABLED = os.environ.get(\"HARNESS_EVICT\", \"1\") != \"0\"\n74\t# **Task-length gate — the primary accuracy & anti-disruption protector.**\n75\t# Eviction does NOT run at all until the run has passed this many turns. Eviction\n76\t# is mildly DISRUPTIVE to this GLM agent: when a doc it is using turns into a\n77\t# stub it may re-read / re-orient, costing extra turns. On a SHORT/medium task\n78\t# (issue-spotting, extraction) that disruption dominates any saving AND risks a\n79\t# dropped fact — and a dev re-fetch blowup confirmed it (a 17-turn extraction\n80\t# task that drifted past a turn-20 gate got disrupted into a 38-turn, 4.4×-token\n81\t# run).          return None\n135\t        return f\"{name}:{pat}:{path}\"\n136\t    return None\n137\t\n138\t\n139\tdef _arg_value(arguments, key):\n140\t    \"\"\"Best-effort extract a named argument from a   if isinstance(arguments, dict):\n146\t            return arguments.get(key)\n147\t    except Exception:\n148\t        pass\n149\t    return None\n150\t\n151\t\n152\tdef _make_stub(name: str, Dicts/lists are mutated in place; returns\n181\t    the (possibly new) value so the caller can reassign str leaves.\"\"\"\n182\t    if isinstance(obj, dict):\n183\t        for k, v in obj.items():\n184\t            obj[k] = _deep_replace(v, old, new)\n185\t        return obj\n186\t    if isinstance(obj, list):\n187\t        for i, v in enumerate(obj):\n188\t            obj[i] = _deep_replace(v, old, new)\n189\t        return obj\n190\t    if isinstance(obj, str):\n191\t        return obj.replace(old, new) if old in obj else obj\n192\t    return obj\n193\t\n194\t\n195\tdef _evict_aged_results(tool_log, current_turn: int,\n196\t                        sticky_keys: set, evicted_keys: set,\n197\t                        evict_state: dict) -> None:\n198\t    \"\"\"Replace large raw tool outputs older than the recent window with a\n199\t    re-read handle, in place, in the message objects already in `messages`.\n200\t\n201\t    `tool_log` is a list of records, one per turn that produced tool results:\n202\t        {\"turn\": int, \"messages\": [<adapter message objects>],\n203\t         \"items\": [{\"name\",\"args\",\"full\",\"evicted\"}]}\n204\t    The message objects in `record[\"messages\"]` are the very objects that live\n205\t    in the loop's `messages` list, so mutating them shrinks the next prompt.\n206\t\n207\t    `sticky_keys` / `evicted_keys` are output identities (see `_evict_key`) the\n208\t    agent has, respectively, re-fetched after an eviction (never evict again) and\n209\t    had evicted at least once (so a future re-fetch becomes sticky and counts\n210\t    toward the kill-switch). `evict_state` carries the run-level kill-switch\n211\t    (`{\"disabled\": bool, \"refetches\": int}`).\n212\t    \"\"\"\n213\t    if not _EVICT_ENABLED or evict_state.get(\"disabled\"):\n214\t        return\n215\t\n216\t    # Task-length gate: leave SHORT/medium runs exactly like bare. agent loop — model calls tools until it finishes or hits max turns.\n\nThis is the core of the harness. It's deliberately simple: the model does\nthe thinking, the loop just shuttles messages back and forth.\n\nThe agent finishes when it stops making tool calls (no explicit `finish`\ntool). The agent loop ends on:\n  1. No tool calls returned — the model has nothing more to do\n  2. Max turns reached\n\n── Carried-context eviction (cost mechanism) ─────────────────────────────\nThe agent is input-bound: every tool result it has ever seen rides along on\nevery later turn's prompt, so the same large raw documents are re-sent turn\nafter turn. That re-carried bulk dominates cost (a single task can run\nmillions of input tokens vs. tens of thousands of output).\n\nThis loop evicts *aged, large* raw tool outputs (`read`/`bash`) from the\ncarried message history, replacing each with a compact **re-read handle**: a\none-line stub naming the tool + file/command and telling the agent how to\nfetch the bytes back on demand. Accuracy is preserved because the document was\nalready read **in full** when it was current (facts in late schedules/tables\nwere seen); we only stop *re-carrying* the raw bytes once they have aged out of\nthe recent working window. If the agent needs the exact text again it re-reads\n— a fresh, full result re-enters context.\n\nDesign points that keep this safe and bounded:\n  - **Task-length gate (the primary accuracy protector).** Eviction does NOT run\n    at all until the run passes EVICT_MIN_TURN turns. The accuracy-fragile tasks\n    here are SHORT issue-spotting / extraction runs that read a few docs and need\n    every fact for a write-up that lands within ~18-20 turns; they finish under\n    the gate and so behave EXACTLY like bare — zero accuracy risk, and there were\n    no carried-context dollars to recover there anyway. Only the genuinely LONG\n    drafting / redline runs (30-120 turns, millions of carried tokens) cross the\n    gate and shed their aged raw docs across the long tail — which is the cost.\n  - **Size gate.** Even past the length gate, eviction is skipped until resident\n    raw output exceeds SIZE_GATE_CHARS (no cost to recover otherwise).\n  - Only outputs older than RECENT_WINDOW turns are eligible (the agent has had\n    a full working window with the doc resident to extract what it needs).\n  - Only outputs larger than MIN_EVICT_CHARS are touched (small results stay).\n  - **Sticky re-fetches + kill-switch (the thrash protector).** An output is\n    evicted at most *once*; a re-fetch of an evicted output (re-read of a file,\n    re-run of a bash/grep/glob, keyed on a stable identity — see `_evict_key`)\n    pins it sticky so it is never evicted again. Beyond that, once the run\n    accumulates EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT re-fetches, eviction is DISABLED for the rest\n    of the run: the task has demonstrated it works against resident outputs (the\n    clause-by-clause redline pattern), so we stop the evict→re-fetch churn before\n    it can run the turn count away (keeps turns < 3× bare).\n  - The task (system + user messages) and the agent's own reasoning/draft\n    output are NEVER evicted — only raw tool results.\n  - Eviction adds no model turns directly; it only shrinks the prompt.\n  - Wrapped in try/except: any failure degrades to plain bare behavior, never\n    crashes the run.\n\nTunable via env (defaults are conservative):\n  HARNESS_EVICT=0                  disable eviction entirely (bare behavior)\n  HARNESS_EVICT_MINTURN=<n>        don't evict until the run passes n turns\n  HARNESS_EVICT_WINDOW=<n>         keep the last n turns of tool results in full\n  HARNESS_EVICT_MINCHARS=<n>       only evict results larger than n chars\n  HARNESS_EVICT_SIZEGATE=<n>       only evict once resident raw output exceeds n\n  HARNESS_EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT=<n>  disable eviction after n re-fetches in a run\n\"\"\"\n\nimport os\nimport time\nimport json\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nfrom harness.adapters.base import ModelAdapter, ModelResponse\nfrom harness.tools import ToolExecutor, get_all_tool_definitions\n\n\n# ── Eviction configuration ────────────────────────────────────────────────\n_EVICT_ENABLED = os.environ.get(\"HARNESS_EVICT\", \"1\") != \"0\"\n# **Task-length gate — the primary accuracy & anti-disruption protector.**\n# Eviction does NOT run at all until the run has passed this many turns. Eviction\n# is mildly DISRUPTIVE to this GLM agent: when a doc it is using turns into a\n# stub it may re-read / re-orient, costing extra turns. On a SHORT/medium task\n# (issue-spotting, extraction) that disruption dominates any saving AND risks a\n# dropped fact — and a dev re-fetch blowup confirmed it (a 17-turn extraction\n# task that drifted past a turn-20 gate got disrupted into a 38-turn, 4.4×-token\n# run). So the gate is set HIGH (28): small/medium tasks finish well under it even\n# on a variance-heavy run, so they never trigger eviction and behave EXACTLY like\n# bare (zero risk, ~zero cost to recover anyway). Only the genuinely HUGE runs\n# (48-120 turns, millions of carried tokens — the cost-dominant redlines/drafts)\n# cross the gate and shed their aged raw docs across the long tail.\n_EVICT_MIN_TURN = int(os.environ.get(\"HARNESS_EVICT_MINTURN\", \"28\"))\n# Within a long run, a doc is only evicted after it has been resident this many\n# turns — the agent has had a full working window with it current to extract\n# what it needs before the raw bytes stop being re-carried.\n_RECENT_WINDOW = int(os.environ.get(\"HARNESS_EVICT_WINDOW\", \"12\"))\n_MIN_EVICT_CHARS = int(os.environ.get(\"HARNESS_EVICT_MINCHARS\", \"6000\"))\n# A low floor: skip eviction entirely on genuinely tiny tasks (resident raw\n# output under this many chars), where there is no cost to recover.\n_SIZE_GATE_CHARS = int(os.environ.get(\"HARNESS_EVICT_SIZEGATE\", \"250000\"))\n# **Re-fetch kill-switch (thrash protector) — disable on the FIRST re-fetch.**\n# A re-fetch of a previously-evicted output (a re-read of an evicted file, or a\n# re-run of an evicted bash/grep/glob) means this task needs its outputs resident\n# — exactly the clause-by-clause redline pattern. Once the run accumulates this\n# many re-fetch events, eviction is DISABLED for the remainder of the run (the\n# re-fetched output is also pinned sticky). Set to 1 so the VERY FIRST re-fetch\n# turns eviction off: this bounds eviction's worst-case overhead to a single\n# extra read (one re-orientation), making a re-fetch LOOP impossible by\n# construction (a 4.4×-token dev blowup under the old limit=2 motivated this), and\n# makes eviction self-targeting — redline tasks that re-read revert to bare almost\n# immediately, while read-then-draft tasks that never re-read keep the full win.\n_EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT = int(os.environ.get(\"HARNESS_EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT\", \"1\"))\n# Tools whose raw output is large and safely re-fetchable on demand.\n_EVICTABLE_TOOLS = {\"read\", \"bash\", \"grep\", \"glob\"}\n\n\ndef _evict_key(name: str, arguments):\n    \"\"\"Stable identity for sticky/evicted tracking across all evictable tools, so\n    a re-fetch of the same output reliably cancels further eviction churn.\n      - read: the file's basename (so \"x.docx\", \"documents/x.docx\", an absolute\n        path all map together).\n      - bash: the stripped command string.\n      - grep/glob: the pattern + path.\n    Returns None when no stable key can be derived (such calls are never pinned\n    and never counted as re-fetches).\"\"\"\n    if name == \"read\":\n        fp = _arg_value(arguments, \"file_path\")\n        if not isinstance(fp, str) or not fp:\n            return None\n        return \"read:\" + fp.rstrip(\"/\").rsplit(\"/\", 1)[-1]\n    if name == \"bash\":\n        cmd = _arg_value(arguments, \"command\")\n        if not isinstance(cmd, str) or not cmd.strip():\n            return None\n        return \"bash:\" + cmd.strip()\n    if name in (\"grep\", \"glob\"):\n        pat = _arg_value(arguments, \"pattern\")\n        path = _arg_value(arguments, \"path\") or \"\"\n        if not isinstance(pat, str) or not pat:\n            return None\n        return f\"{name}:{pat}:{path}\"\n    return None\n\n\ndef _arg_value(arguments, key):\n    \"\"\"Best-effort extract a named argument from a tool call's arguments,\n    which may be a dict or a JSON string.\"\"\"\n    try:\n        if isinstance(arguments, str):\n            arguments = json.loads(arguments)\n        if isinstance(arguments, dict):\n            return arguments.get(key)\n    except Exception:\n        pass\n    return None\n\n\ndef _make_stub(name: str, arguments, full: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"A compact re-read handle that replaces an evicted raw tool output.\"\"\"\n    approx_tok = max(1, len(full) // 4)\n    if name == \"read\":\n        fp = _arg_value(arguments, \"file_path\") or \"the same file\"\n        return (\n            f\"[context-saver: the full output of read(file_path={fp!r}) \"\n            f\"(~{approx_tok:,} tokens) was already read in full and has been \"\n            f\"elided here to keep the running context small. If you still need \"\n            f\"its exact text, call read on {fp!r} again to bring it back.]\"\n        )\n    if name == \"bash\":\n        cmd = (_arg_value(arguments, \"command\") or \"\").strip().replace(\"\\n\", \" \")\n        snippet = (cmd[:120] + \"…\") if len(cmd) > 120 else cmd\n        return (\n            f\"[context-saver: the full output (~{approx_tok:,} tokens) of bash \"\n            f\"command `{snippet}` has been elided to keep context small. \"\n            f\"Re-run the command if you need its output again.]\"\n        )\n    # grep / glob / anything else\n    return (\n        f\"[context-saver: a large {name} result (~{approx_tok:,} tokens) has \"\n        f\"been elided to keep context small. Re-run the {name} if you need it.]\"\n    )\n\n\ndef _deep_replace(obj, old: str, new: str):\n    \"\"\"Recursively replace occurrences of `old` with `new` in str leaves of a\n    (possibly nested) message object. Dicts/lists are mutated in place; returns\n    the (possibly new) value so the caller can reassign str leaves.\"\"\"\n    if isinstance(obj, dict):\n        for k, v in obj.items():\n            obj[k] = _deep_replace(v, old, new)\n        return obj\n    if isinstance(obj, list):\n        for i, v in enumerate(obj):\n            obj[i] = _deep_replace(v, old, new)\n        return obj\n    if isinstance(obj, str):\n        return obj.replace(old, new) if old in obj else obj\n    return obj\n\n\ndef _evict_aged_results(tool_log, current_turn: int,\n                        sticky_keys: set, evicted_keys: set,\n                        evict_state: dict) -> None:\n    \"\"\"Replace large raw tool outputs older than the recent window with a\n    re-read handle, in place, in the message objects already in `messages`.\n\n    `tool_log` is a list of records, one per turn that produced tool results:\n        {\"turn\": int, \"messages\": [<adapter message objects>],\n         \"items\": [{\"name\",\"args\",\"full\",\"evicted\"}]}\n    The message objects in `record[\"messages\"]` are the very objects that live\n    in the loop's `messages` list, so mutating them shrinks the next prompt.\n\n    `sticky_keys` / `evicted_keys` are output identities (see `_evict_key`) the\n    agent has, respectively, re-fetched after an eviction (never evict again) and\n    had evicted at least once (so a future re-fetch becomes sticky and counts\n    toward the kill-switch). `evict_state` carries the run-level kill-switch\n    (`{\"disabled\": bool, \"refetches\": int}`).\n    \"\"\"\n    if not _EVICT_ENABLED or evict_state.get(\"disabled\"):\n        return\n\n    # Task-length gate: leave SHORT/medium runs exactly like bare. Only genuinely\n    # long runs (where the carried-context dollars live) ever shed raw outputs.\n    if current_turn <= _EVICT_MIN_TURN:\n        return\n\n    # Size gate: how many chars of raw evictable output are currently resident?\n    # If we're under the gate, there is no cost to recover — behave like bare.\n    resident = 0\n    for rec in tool_log:\n        for item in rec[\"items\"]:\n            if item[\"evicted\"]:\n                continue\n            full = item[\"full\"]\n            if isinstance(full, str) and item[\"name\"] in _EVICTABLE_TOOLS:\n                resident += len(full)\n    if resident < _SIZE_GATE_CHARS:\n        return\n\n    for rec in tool_log:\n        if current_turn - rec[\"turn\"] < _RECENT_WINDOW:\n            continue  # still in the fresh working window — keep full\n        for item in rec[\"items\"]:\n            if item[\"evicted\"]:\n                continue\n            full = item[\"full\"]\n            if (not isinstance(full, str) or len(full) < _MIN_EVICT_CHARS\n                    or item[\"name\"] not in _EVICTABLE_TOOLS):\n                item[\"evicted\"] = True  # never eligible; stop reconsidering\n                continue\n            # Sticky outputs (re-fetched after a prior eviction) stay resident.\n            key = _evict_key(item[\"name\"], item[\"args\"])\n            if key is not None and key in sticky_keys:\n                item[\"evicted\"] = True  # resolved: leave full, never reconsider\n                continue\n            stub = _make_stub(item[\"name\"], item[\"args\"], full)\n            for msg in rec[\"messages\"]:\n                _deep_replace(msg, full, stub)\n            item[\"evicted\"] = True\n            item[\"full\"] = None  # free memory; we won't need it again\n            if key is not None:\n                evicted_keys.add(key)  # a future re-fetch of this -> sticky\n\n\ndef run_agent(\n    adapter: ModelAdapter,\n    system_prompt: str,\n    user_prompt: str,\n    tool_executor: ToolExecutor,\n    tools: list[dict] | None = None,\n    max_turns: int = 200,\n    transcript_path: str | None = None,\n) -> dict:\n    \"\"\"Run the agent loop to completion.\n\n    Args:\n        adapter: The model adapter (Anthropic, OpenAI, Google, xAI).\n        system_prompt: Capabilities and conventions (preamble + skill manuals).\n        user_prompt: The first user message — the task assignment.\n        tool_executor: Configured tool executor with documents and output dirs.\n        tools: Tool definitions to use. Defaults to standard 6 tools if not provided.\n        max_turns: Maximum number of loop iterations.\n        transcript_path: Optional path to write transcript JSONL.\n\n    Returns:\n        Dict with run results: messages, metrics, timing.\n    \"\"\"\n    messages = [\n        adapter.make_system_message(system_prompt),\n        adapter.make_user_message(user_prompt),\n    ]\n    if tools is None:\n        tools = get_all_tool_definitions()\n\n    total_input_tokens = 0\n    total_output_tokens = 0\n    total_cache_read = 0\n    total_cache_creation = 0\n    turn_count = 0\n    start_time = time.time()\n\n    # Per-turn records of tool-result messages, used to evict aged raw outputs\n    # from the carried context (see module docstring).\n    tool_log: list[dict] = []\n    evicted_keys: set[str] = set()   # output identities evicted at least once\n    sticky_keys: set[str] = set()    # identities re-fetched after eviction -> keep\n    # Run-level kill-switch: after _EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT re-fetches the task has\n    # shown it needs its outputs resident, so eviction stops for the rest of the\n    # run (bounds any evict→re-fetch loop / turn-count blowup).\n    evict_state: dict = {\"disabled\": False, \"refetches\": 0}\n\n    transcript_file = None\n    if transcript_path:\n        Path(transcript_path).parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)\n        transcript_file = open(transcript_path, \"w\")\n        print(json.dumps({\"turn\": 0, \"role\": \"system\", \"text\": system_prompt}), file=transcript_file)\n        print(json.dumps({\"turn\": 0, \"role\": \"user\", \"text\": user_prompt}), file=transcript_file)\n        transcript_file.flush()\n\n    context_overflow = False\n    try:\n        for turn in range(max_turns):\n            turn_count = turn + 1\n\n            # Evict aged, large raw tool outputs from the carried context before\n            # sending the next prompt. Never let a compaction bug crash the run.\n            try:\n                _evict_aged_results(tool_log, turn_count, sticky_keys,\n                                    evicted_keys, evict_state)\n            except Exception as e:\n                print(f\"[evict] skipped on turn {turn_count}: {type(e).__name__}: {e}\")\n\n            # Call the model\n            try:\n                response = adapter.chat(messages, tools)\n            except Exception as e:\n                err_msg = str(e)\n                if \"prompt is too long\" in err_msg or \"context_length_exceeded\" in err_msg:\n                    context_overflow = True\n                    print(f\"Context window exceeded on turn {turn_count}: {err_msg}\")\n                    break\n                raise\n\n            messages.append(response.message)\n            total_input_tokens += response.input_tokens\n            total_output_tokens += response.output_tokens\n            total_cache_read += response.cache_read_input_tokens\n            total_cache_creation += response.cache_creation_input_tokens\n\n            # Log to transcript\n            if transcript_file:\n                _log_turn(transcript_file, turn_count, \"assistant\", response)\n\n            # If no tool calls, the agent is done\n            if not response.tool_calls:\n                break\n\n            # Execute each tool call and feed results back\n            tool_results = []\n            for tc in response.tool_calls:\n                result = tool_executor.execute(tc.name, tc.arguments)\n\n                if transcript_file:\n                    _log_tool(transcript_file, turn_count, tc.name, tc.arguments, result)\n\n                tool_results.append((tc, result))\n\n            # Add tool results to message history via the adapter\n            result_messages = adapter.make_tool_result_messages(\n                [(tc.id, result) for tc, result in tool_results]\n            )\n            messages.extend(result_messages)\n\n            # A re-fetch of a previously-evicted output (re-read of an evicted\n            # file, or re-run of an evicted bash/grep/glob) means the agent needs\n            # it resident — pin it sticky so it is never evicted again, and count\n            # it toward the run-level kill-switch. Once enough re-fetches\n            # accumulate, eviction is disabled for the rest of the run so an\n            # evict→re-fetch pattern can never run the turn count away.\n            for tc, _result in tool_results:\n                key = _evict_key(tc.name, tc.arguments)\n                if key is not None and key in evicted_keys:\n                    sticky_keys.add(key)\n                    evict_state[\"refetches\"] += 1\n                    if evict_state[\"refetches\"] >= _EVICT_REFETCH_LIMIT:\n                        evict_state[\"disabled\"] = True\n\n            # Record these tool-result messages so aged, large raw outputs can\n            # be evicted later. start_time\n\n    return {\n        \"messages\": messages,\n        \"turn_count\": turn_count,\n        \"input_tokens\": total_input_tokens,\n        \"output_tokens\": total_output_tokens,\n        \"cache_read_input_tokens\": total_cache_read,\n        \"cache_creation_input_tokens\": total_cache_creation,\n        \"wall_clock_seconds\": round(elapsed, 2),\n        \"finished_cleanly\": (not context_overflow and\n                             (not response.tool_calls if turn_count > 0 else False)),\n        \"context_overflow\": context_overflow,\n        \"tool_metrics\": tool_executor.get_metrics(),\n        \"finish_summary\": None,\n    }\n\n\ndef _log_turn(f, turn: int, role: str, response: ModelResponse):\n    \"\"\"Log a turn to the transcript JSONL.\"\"\"\n    entry = {\n        \"turn\": turn,\n        \"role\": role,\n        \"text\": response.text if response.text else None,\n        \"tool_calls\": [\n            {\"name\": tc.name, \"arguments\": tc.arguments}\n            for tc in response.tool_calls\n        ] if response.tool_calls else None,\n        \"input_tokens\": response.input_tokens,\n        \"output_tokens\": response.output_tokens,\n        \"cache_read_input_tokens\": response.cache_read_input_tokens,\n        \"cache_creation_input_tokens\": response.cache_creation_input_tokens,\n    }\n    f.write(json.dumps(entry) + \"\\n\")\n    f.flush()\n\n\ndef _log_tool(f, turn: int, name: str, arguments: str, result: str):\n    \"\"\"Log a tool execution to the transcript JSONL.\"\"\"\n    entry = {\n        \"turn\": turn,\n        \"role\": \"tool\",\n        \"tool_name\": name,\n        \"arguments\": arguments if isinstance(arguments, str) else str(arguments),\n        \"result_preview\": result[:1000],\n        \"result\": result,\n    }\n    f.write(json.dumps(entry) + \"\\n\")\n    f.flush()\n","numLines":448,"startLine":1,"totalLines":448}}}

The caller owns its lifecycle (start/stop).\n213\t\n214\t      ToolExecutor(documents_dir=..., output_dir=..., workspace_dir=..., ...)\n215\t          Convenience: builds and starts a sandbox internally and tears it\n216\t          down in close(). Creates parent directories if \"\n            \"needed.\"\n        ),\n        \"parameters\": {\n            \"type\": \"object\",\n            \"properties\": {\n                \"file_path\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"Relative path under the output directory (e.g., 'response.md')\",\n                },\n                \"content\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"Markdown content to write\",\n                },\n            },\n            \"required\": [\"file_path\", \"content\"],\n        },\n    },\n    {\n        \"name\": \"edit\",\n        \"description\": (\n            \"Perform exact string replacement in a file you have already \"\n            \"created or read. The old_string must appear exactly once unless \"\n            \"replace_all is true. Use for incremental refinement, not \"\n            \"first-time writes.\"\n        ),\n        \"parameters\": {\n            \"type\": \"object\",\n            \"properties\": {\n                \"file_path\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"Path to the file to modify\",\n                },\n                \"old_string\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"The exact text to find and replace\",\n                },\n                \"new_string\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"The replacement text\",\n                },\n                \"replace_all\": {\n                    \"type\": \"boolean\",\n                    \"description\": \"If true, replace all occurrences. Default false.\",\n                    \"default\": False,\n                },\n            },\n            \"required\": [\"file_path\", \"old_string\", \"new_string\"],\n        },\n    },\n    {\n        \"name\": \"glob\",\n        \"description\": (\n            \"Find files matching a glob pattern, sorted by modification time. \"\n            \"Defaults to searching the input directory. Prefer this over \"\n            \"`bash find` or `bash ls` for file discovery.\"\n        ),\n        \"parameters\": {\n            \"type\": \"object\",\n            \"properties\": {\n                \"pattern\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"Glob pattern to match (e.g., '**/*.docx', 'src/**/*.py')\",\n                },\n                \"path\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"Directory to search in. Defaults to the input directory.\",\n                },\n            },\n            \"required\": [\"pattern\"],\n        },\n    },\n    {\n        \"name\": \"grep\",\n        \"description\": (\n            \"Search file contents using regex patterns. Defaults to searching \"\n            \"the input directory. Returns matching file paths or matching \"\n            \"lines with context.\"\n        ),\n        \"parameters\": {\n            \"type\": \"object\",\n            \"properties\": {\n                \"pattern\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"Regex pattern to search for\",\n                },\n                \"path\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"File or directory to search in. Defaults to the input directory.\",\n                },\n                \"glob\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"description\": \"Glob pattern to filter files (e.g., '*.py', '*.docx')\",\n                },\n                \"output_mode\": {\n                    \"type\": \"string\",\n                    \"enum\": [\"content\", \"files_with_matches\", \"count\"],\n                    \"description\": (\n                        \"Output format. 'content' shows matching lines, \"\n                        \"'files_with_matches' shows file paths, 'count' shows \"\n                        \"match counts. Default: 'files_with_matches'.\"\n                    ),\n                },\n            },\n            \"required\": [\"pattern\"],\n        },\n    },\n]\n\n\ndef get_all_tool_definitions() -> list[dict]:\n    \"\"\"Get all tool definitions.\"\"\"\n    return list(TOOL_DEFINITIONS)\n\n\n# ── Tool Executor ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\n\nclass ToolExecutor:\n    \"\"\"Executes tool calls against a per-task Sandbox.\n\n    Two construction modes:\n\n      ToolExecutor(sandbox=sb, ...)\n          Use a pre-built sandbox. The caller owns its lifecycle (start/stop).\n\n      ToolExecutor(documents_dir=..., output_dir=..., workspace_dir=..., ...)\n          Convenience: builds and starts a sandbox internally and tears it\n          down in close(). Convenient for tests and one-off scripts.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        documents_dir: str | None = None,\n        output_dir: str | None = None,\n        workspace_dir: str | None = None,\n        shell_timeout: int = 60,\n        sandbox: Sandbox | None = None,\n    ):\n        if sandbox is not None:\n            if documents_dir or output_dir or workspace_dir:\n                raise ValueError(\n                    \"pass either `sandbox` or the (documents_dir, output_dir, \"\n                    \"workspace_dir) tuple — not both\"\n                )\n            self.sandbox = sandbox\n            self._owns_sandbox = False\n        else:\n            if documents_dir is None or output_dir is None:\n                raise ValueError(\"documents_dir and output_dir are required\")\n            self.sandbox = Sandbox(\n                documents_dir=Path(documents_dir),\n                output_dir=Path(output_dir),\n                workspace_dir=Path(workspace_dir) if workspace_dir else Path(output_dir),\n                default_timeout=shell_timeout,\n            )\n            self.sandbox.start()\n            self._owns_sandbox = True\n\n        # Cache the host paths for parts that still need them (document\n        # parsing libraries that take filesystem paths, metric reporting).\n        self.documents_dir = self.sandbox.documents_dir\n        self.output_dir = self.sandbox.output_dir\n        self.workspace_dir = self.sandbox.workspace_dir\n        self.shell_timeout = shell_timeout\n\n        # Track usage for metrics.\n        self.files_read: list[str] = []\n        self.files_written: int = 0\n        self.files_edited: int = 0\n        self.bash_command_count: int = 0\n        self.glob_count: int = 0\n        self.grep_count: int = 0\n\n    def close(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Tear down the sandbox if we own it. Idempotent.\"\"\"\n        if self._owns_sandbox and self.sandbox is not None:\n            self.sandbox.stop()\n            self._owns_sandbox = False\n\n    def __enter__(self):\n        return self\n\n    def __exit__(self, exc_type, exc, tb):\n        self.close()\n\n    def __del__(self):\n        try:\n            self.close()\n        except Exception:\n            pass\n\n    # ── Path Resolution ───────────────────────────────────────────────\n\n    def _resolve_read_path(self, path_str: str) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Resolve to a sandbox-relative path. Checks workspace, documents, output.\n\n        - Absolute sandbox paths (`/workspace/documents/...`) are validated and passed through.\n        - Relative paths probe /workspace, /workspace/documents, /workspace/output in that\n          order, falling back to /workspace/documents if nothing exists yet (matches\n          legacy behavior).\n        \"\"\"\n        if path_str.startswith(\"/\"):\n            Sandbox.assert_sandbox_path(path_str)\n            return path_str\n        # Relative — probe each mount.\n        for mount in (WORKSPACE_PATH, DOCUMENTS_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH):\n            candidate = f\"{mount}/{path_str}\"\n            if self.sandbox.exists(candidate):\n                return candidate\n        # Default to documents (matches legacy fallback).\n        return f\"{DOCUMENTS_PATH}/{path_str}\"\n\n    def _resolve_write_path(self, path_str: str) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Resolve to a sandbox-relative writable path.\n\n        - Absolute sandbox paths under /workspace/output or /workspace (excluding\n          /workspace/documents) pass through.\n        - Relative paths are written under /workspace/output.\n        \"\"\"\n        if path_str.startswith(\"/\"):\n            Sandbox.assert_sandbox_path(path_str)\n            if not Sandbox.is_writable(path_str):\n                raise PermissionError(\n                    f\"write denied: {path_str} is read-only \"\n                    f\"(documents) or outside /workspace\"\n                )\n            return path_str\n        return f\"{OUTPUT_PATH}/{path_str}\"\n\n    def _resolve_search_path(self, path_str: str | None) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Resolve glob/grep search root to a sandbox-relative path.\"\"\"\n        if not path_str:\n            return DOCUMENTS_PATH\n        if path_str.startswith(\"/\"):\n            Sandbox.assert_sandbox_path(path_str)\n            return path_str\n        for mount in (DOCUMENTS_PATH, WORKSPACE_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH):\n            candidate = f\"{mount}/{path_str}\"\n            if self.sandbox.exists(candidate):\n                return candidate\n        return f\"{DOCUMENTS_PATH}/{path_str}\"\n\n    # ── Dispatch ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\n    def execute(self, tool_name: str, arguments: str | dict) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Execute a tool call and return the result as a string.\"\"\"\n        if isinstance(arguments, str):\n            try:\n                arguments = json.loads(arguments)\n            except json.JSONDecodeError:\n                return f\"Error: invalid JSON arguments: {arguments}\"\n\n        try:\n            if tool_name == \"bash\":\n                return self._bash(arguments.get(\"command\", \"\"))\n            elif tool_name == \"read\":\n                return self._read(\n                    arguments.get(\"file_path\", \"\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"offset\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"limit\"),\n                )\n            elif tool_name == \"write\":\n                return self._write(\n                    arguments.get(\"file_path\", \"\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"content\", \"\"),\n                )\n            elif tool_name == \"edit\":\n                return self._edit(\n                    arguments.get(\"file_path\", \"\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"old_string\", \"\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"new_string\", \"\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"replace_all\", False),\n                )\n            elif tool_name == \"glob\":\n                return self._glob(\n                    arguments.get(\"pattern\", \"\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"path\"),\n                )\n            elif tool_name == \"grep\":\n                return self._grep(\n                    arguments.get(\"pattern\", \"\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"path\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"glob\"),\n                    arguments.get(\"output_mode\", \"files_with_matches\"),\n                )\n\n            return     except ValueError as e:\n            # Sandbox path discipline violations (e.g. \"/tmp/foo\" passed to\n            # read/write) raise ValueError. Return as a tool error so the\n            # agent can self-correct rather than crashing the run.\n            return f\"Error: {e}\"\n        except Exception as e:\n            # Final safety net: every tool call returns a string to the\n            # agent, no exception escapes this boundary. Without this,\n            # a corrupt .docx, a transient podman hiccup, a disk-full\n            # OSError, etc. would crash the run mid-flight. Surfacing the\n            # exception type lets the agent reason about whether to retry,\n            # try a different tool, or give up on a particular file.\n            return f\"Error: {type(e).__name__}: {e}\"\n\n    # ── Tool Implementations ──────────────────────────────────────────\n\n    def _bash(self, command: str) -> str:\n        if not command:\n            return \"Error: command is required\"\n\n        self.bash_command_count += 1\n        result = self.sandbox.exec(command, timeout=self.shell_timeout)\n\n        output = result.stdout\n        if result.stderr:\n            output += f\"\\nSTDERR:\\n{result.stderr}\"\n        if result.timed_out:\n            return f\"Error: command timed out after {self.shell_timeout}s\\n{output}\"\n        if result.returncode is not None and result.returncode != 0:\n            output += f\"\\n(exit code {result.returncode})\"\n        return output or \"(no output)\"\n\n    def _read(self, file_path: str, offset: int | None, limit: int | None) -> str:\n        if not file_path:\n            return \"Error: file_path is required\"\n\n        sb_path = self._resolve_read_path(file_path)\n        if not self.sandbox.exists(sb_path):\n            return f\"Error: file not found: {file_path}\"\n\n        # This keeps attacker-controlled\n        document content from being parsed by host Python — pdfplumber /\n        pandas / markitdown have a non-trivial vulnerability surface.\n\n        Plain text and everything else uses sandbox.read_file().\n\n        Parser failures (corrupt .docx, encrypted .pdf, etc.) come back as\n        error strings so the agent can pivot to other documents rather\n        than crashing the run.\n        \"\"\"\n        suffix = Path(sb_path).suffix.lower()\n        ext = suffix[1:]  # Quote the path for the shell — sandbox paths shouldn't contain\n        # spaces or shell metas in practice, but defense in depth.\n        result = self.sandbox.exec(\n            f\"parse-doc {ext} {shlex.quote(sb_path)}\",\n            timeout=120,  # Symlink-escape is\n        guarded via `_is_under` at the read step.\n        \"\"\"\n        if sb_path.startswith(DOCUMENTS_PATH):\n            rel = sb_path[len(DOCUMENTS_PATH):].lstrip(\"/\")\n {sb_path}\")\n\n    def _write(self, file_path: str, content: str) -> str:\n        if not file_path:\n            return \"Error: file_path is required\"\n\n        sb_path = _edit(self, file_path: str, old_string: str, new_string: str, replace_all: bool) -> str:\n        if not file_path:\n            return \"Error: file_path is required\"\n\n        # Locate the file: writable mounts first (the agent is editing its\n        # own output), then the wider read locations.\n        if file_path.startswith(\"/\"):\n            Sandbox.assert_sandbox_path(file_path)\n            sb_path = file_path\n        else:\n            sb_path = None\n            for mount in (OUTPUT_PATH, WORKSPACE_PATH, DOCUMENTS_PATH):\n                candidate = f\"{mount}/{file_path}\"\n                if self.sandbox.exists(candidate):\n                    sb_path = candidate\n                    break\n            if sb_path is None:\n                return f\"Error: file not found: {file_path}\"\n\n        if not Sandbox.is_writable(sb_path):\n            return f\"SecurityError: write denied: {sb_path} is not under a writable mount\"\n        if not self.sandbox.exists(sb_path):\n            return f\"Error: file not found: {file_path}\"\n\n        text = self.sandbox.read_file(sb_path).decode(\"utf-8\", errors=\"replace\")\n        count = text.count(old_string)\n        if count == 0:\n            return f\"Error: old_string not found in {file_path}\"\n        if count > 1 and not replace_all:\n            return (\n                f\"Error: old_string found {count} times in {file_path}. \"\n                \"Use replace_all=true to replace all.\"\n            )\n\n        new_text = text.replace(old_string, new_string) if replace_all \\\n            else text.replace(old_string, new_string, 1)\n\n        self.sandbox.write_file(sb_path, new_text)\n        self.files_edited += 1\n        replaced = count if replace_all else 1\n        return f\"Replaced {replaced} occurrence(s) in {file_path}\"\n\n    def _glob(self, pattern: str, search_path: str | None) -> str:\n        if not pattern:\n            return \"Error: pattern is required\"\n\n        self.glob_count += 1\n\n        sb_path = self._resolve_search_path(search_path)\n        if not self.sandbox.exists(sb_path):\n            return f\"Error: path does not exist: {search_path}\"\n\n        # We need ordering by mtime — easiest to do that on the host since\n        # both backends bind-mount the same dirs.\n        host_root = self._sandbox_to_host_path(sb_path) if sb_path != \"/\" else self.documents_dir\n        if not host_root.exists():\n            return f\"Error: path does not exist: {search_path}\"\n\n        host_root_resolved = host_root.resolve(strict=False)\n        matches = sorted(\n            (m for m in host_root.glob(pattern)\n             if m.is_file() and self._is_under(m, host_root_resolved)),\n            key=lambda p: p.stat().st_mtime,\n            reverse=True,\n        )\n        if not matches:\n            return f\"No files matching '{pattern}' in {sb_path}\"\n str) -> str:\n        if not pattern_str:\n            return \"Error: pattern is required\"\n\n        self.grep_count += 1\n\n        sb_path = self._resolve_search_path(search_path)\n        if not self.sandbox.exists(sb_path):\n            return f\"Error: path does not exist: {search_path}\"\n\n        try:\n            regex = re.compile(pattern_str)\n        except re.error as e:\n self._sandbox_to_host_path(sb_path)\n        host_root_resolved = host_root.resolve(strict=False)\n        glob_pattern = file_glob or \"**/*\"\n        results = []\n\n        for fpath in host_root.glob(glob_pattern):\n            if not fpath.is_file():\n                continue\n            # Reject symlinks (or any path) whose real target escapes the\n            # bind-mount root. Without this, an agent could `ln -s\n            # /etc/passwd /workspace/output/leak` from inside the container,\n            # then call grep — the symlink string is innocent inside the\n            # container, but read_text() runs on the host and resolves\n            # against the host's namespace, leaking host files.\n            if not self._is_under(fpath, host_root_resolved):\n                continue\n            try:\n                text = fpath.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\", errors=\"replace\")\n            except Exception:\n                continue\n            matches = list(regex.finditer(text))\n            if matches:\n                rel = str(fpath.relative_to(host_root))\n                if output_mode == \"files_with_matches\":\n                    results.append(rel)\n                elif output_mode == \"count\":\n                    results.append(f\"{rel}: {len(matches)}\")\n                elif output_mode == \"content\":\n                    lines = text.split(\"\\n\")\n                    for i, line in enumerate(lines):\n                        if regex.search(line):\n                            results.append(f\"{rel}:{i+1}: {line}\")\n\n        return \"\\n\".join(results[:250]) if results else f\"No matches for '{pattern_str}'\"\n\n    @staticmethod\n    def _is_under(fpath: Path, root_resolved: Path) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"True if `fpath` resolves to a real path still under `root_resolved`.\n\n        Used to defeat symlink escapes during host-side glob/grep traversal:\n        an agent that creates `/workspace/output/leak -> /etc/passwd` from\n        inside the container creates a symlink whose host-side resolve\n        target leaves the bind-mount root.\n        \"\"\"\n        try:\n            fpath.resolve(strict=False).relative_to(root_resolved)\n            return True\n        except ValueError:\n            return False\n\n    def get_metrics(self) -> dict:\n        all_documents_files = sorted(\n            str(f.relative_to(self.documents_dir))\n            for f in self.documents_dir.rglob(\"*\")\n            if f.is_file()\n        )\n\n        unique_reads = list(dict.fromkeys(self.files_read))\n        skipped = [f for f in all_documents_files if f not in unique_reads]\n\n        return {\n            \"documents_read\": len(unique_reads),\n {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01RdH7LiDnpTwKAmi4adSWmZ","type":"tool_result","content":"backed up iter2 agent_loop.py\n=== run_harvey_agent.md ===\n# Tool — `run_harvey_agent`\n\n> The mutator invokes this from its shell to run a BATCH of Harvey rollouts concurrently, for triage.\n\n## Purpose\n\nRun the **frozen Harvey agent** on **one or many task ids** (a **batch**, run **concurrently**),\nusing your **current `harness/`**: the broker overlays your edited `system_prompt.md` / `tools.py` /\n`agent_loop.py` onto the bare harvey-labs checkout and runs that (exactly what the standard eval\nwould run), producing a deliverable + trajectory **per task** you can inspect and proxy-grade. This\nis how you *try* a harness edit before the canonical eval sees it — and how you buy **breadth**:\ntest one edit across several tasks in a **single call** (they run in parallel) instead of one slow\nserial rollout at a time.\n\nThe Harvey agent is **frozen** here: this tool does not change the agent, the model, or the\nendpoint — it executes the harness as-is. Your edits to `harness/` are what change the output.\n\n## Interface\n\n- **Input:** one or more `task_id`s from your **TRAIN access set** (the matters under `rollouts/` /\n  the train manifest), space-separated: `run_harvey_agent <task_id> [task_id2 ...]`. The batch runs\n  concurrently (capped at a few at a time). Held-out **val** ids are **not available**; a batch\n  containing **any** non-train id is **refused whole**.\n- **ASYNC — returns immediately, runs in the background.** A batch takes ~15-20 min (each rollout\n  ~9-10 min), longer than the shell's 10-minute cap, so the command **detaches a worker that survives\n  the cap** and returns at once. It prints a **done-marker path** `scratch/runs/.batch_<id>.done`\n  (and a live log). **Workflow: launch → poll `test -f <marker>` → `cat` the marker for the summary →\n  THEN `proxy_eval`.** The deliverables are NOT ready the instant it returns — polling first is\n  required, and it's what prevents the old failure (client killed at 10 min, broker keeps charging,\n  deliverables lost). Don't re-launch the same batch while it's still running — you'd pay twice.\n- **Output (all under `scratch/`):** one dir per task — `scratch/runs/<task_id>/deliverable.md`\n  (pass it to `proxy_eval`) **and `scratch/runs/<task_id>/turns.txt`** (the rollout's turn count) for\n  **`check_runaway`** (the runaway gate) — both written when the batch completes. The done-marker\n  holds the per-task summary (`wrote ... turns=...`, `skipped_for_budget`, or `OVER_BUDGET`); a task\n  that errors is reported there but doesn't sink the rest of the batch.\n- Writes **nothing** outside `scratch/`.\n\n## Cost\n\n≈ **~$1 per task** (one Harvey-agent rollout) × the number of tasks in the batch. **Metered** — see\n`budget.md`; a batch is charged per task only up to the remaining cap (the excess is skipped, not\ncharged). The unit cost is surfaced by the `budget` tool so you can size your batch.\n\n## Guardrails\n\n- **Counts against the budget.** Charged per task, pre-spend. If the **whole** batch is over budget\n  the call returns OVER_BUDGET (your \"commit now\" cue); a partially-over batch runs what fits and\n  returns the rest as `skipped_for_budget`. Check `budget` to size your batch. The budget is there to\n  be **used**: confirm a candidate across **several distinct train tasks in one batch** (and against\n  bare on the same tasks), not a single rollout — breadth across different matters is what shows the\n  edit *generalizes* to tasks you can't see, and it's the main thing to spend the budget on\n  (CLAUDE.md §3). A near-empty ledger means you under-experimented.\n- **Never writes to `rollouts/`.** `rollouts/` is the canonical standard-eval path, owned by the\n  outer driver. This tool is private triage; its outputs are ephemeral `scratch/` artifacts and\n  **must not feed selection**.\n- **Train-only — the val set is unreachable.** Only TRAIN task ids resolve; the held-out val\n  tasks are never mounted into the workspace and any non-train id is refused. Running the agent on\n  a val task would contaminate the held-out verdict, so it is impossible by construction.\n- Frozen agent: do not use this to \"grade your own homework\" — pair it with `proxy_eval` for a\n  cheap private signal only, never as the verdict.\n=== train_baseline keys ===\n['n', 'per_task', 'source']\n{'n': 30}","is_error":false}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4283aaf1-9e61-4711-af01-0dc2c98501ec","uuid":"6bcd2a10-5429-40dc-8a32-775349bd36f2","timestamp":"2026-06-28T20:35:05.171Z","tool_use_result":{"stdout":"backed up iter2 agent_loop.py\n=== run_harvey_agent.md ===\n# Tool — `run_harvey_agent`\n\n> The mutator invokes this from its shell to run a BATCH of Harvey rollouts concurrently, for triage.\n\n## Purpose\n\nRun the **frozen Harvey agent** on **one or many task ids** (a **batch**, run **concurrently**),\nusing your **current `harness/`**: the broker overlays your edited `system_prompt.md` / `tools.py` /\n`agent_loop.py` onto the bare harvey-labs checkout and runs that (exactly what the standard eval\nwould run), producing a deliverable + trajectory **per task** you can inspect and proxy-grade. A near-empty ledger means you under-experimented.\n- **Never writes to `rollouts/`.** `rollouts/` is the canonical standard-eval path, owned by the\n  outer driver. It returns **all three parts of the gate**: the **accuracy** (`dev_score` = mean ensemble\npass-rate), the **cost** (`cost.mean_input_tokens` / `mean_total_tokens` / `mean_turns`, plus per-task\n`input_tokens` / `turns`), and a **per-task THRASH check** — so one call tells you whether accuracy\nheld, cost dropped, AND no single task blew up under the mean.\n\nThis is the signal you should **commit on**. It differs from `proxy_eval` in the two ways that matter:\n\n| | `proxy_eval` | `dev_eval` |\n|---|---|---|\n| tasks | a TRAIN task you tune on | held-out DEV tasks you never tune on |\n| grader | single cheap gpt-5-mini | **ensemble** (same as the real verdict) |\n| use | EXPLORE — rank your own attempts | **DECIDE** — gate the commit |\n\nThe proxy is a fast, biased hint; the ensemble on held-out dev is measured the way the verdict is.\nA high proxy score that does **not** hold up on `dev_eval` is exactly the signal to **not** commit.\n\n## Interface\n\n- **Input:** nothing = the **full** dev set (this is the gate — run it this way). A space-separated\n  subset of **dev** ids is allowed (`dev_eval [task_id ...]`) but is only a **noisy, small-sample**\n  read: it prints a `PARTIAL DEV … SMALL-SAMPLE` banner and must NOT be the basis for a commit (see\n  Guardrails). Every id must be a dev id; any non-dev id (including any val id) refuses the whole call.\n  The held-out val set is unreachable here.\n- **ASYNC — returns immediately, runs in the background.** A full dev eval is ~30 rollouts\n  (~15-25 min), longer than the shell's 10-minute cap, so the command detaches a worker that\n  survives the cap and prints a **done-marker path** `scratch/runs/.dev_<id>.done`.\n  **Workflow: launch → poll `test -f <marker>` → `cat` it for `dev_score` → commit (or not).**\n- **Output** (the marker, read top to bottom):\n  - a `PARTIAL DEV … SMALL-SAMPLE` banner **iff** you ran a subset — a heads-up that this read is a\n    likely-overfit fluke, not a commit signal;\n  - `dev_score=<accuracy>` over `n_graded/n_requested` tasks — the **accuracy gate**;\n  - a `cost:` line (`mean_input_tokens` / `mean_total_tokens` / `mean_turns`) — the **cost objective**;\n  - a `COMMIT only if ALL THREE hold` line (accuracy ≥ bare−noise AND cost clearly below bare AND no\n    per-task THRASH) — the decision rule, restated inline;\n  - a `THRASH CHECK:` block — per dev task, vs the per-task bare dev baseline. **THRASH** = a re-fetch\n    **LOOP** (turns **≥2×** with tokens **≥1.5×**, or tokens **≥3×** with turns **≥1.5×** — a HARD reject); a single-axis rise flagged **≥1.5×** is a **watch**,\n    including a **tokens-only ≥2× with turns ~flat** (a one-time re-read or GLM variance — weigh, don't\n    auto-reject). A task with no bare baseline is reported **cost UNKNOWN** (never silently counted clean).\n  - per-task lines (`acc=`, `in_tok=`, `turns=`). The full structured result is also written to\n    `scratch/dev_eval_<id>.json`.\n\n## Cost\n\n≈ **~$1.10 per dev task** (one rollout ~$1 + one ensemble grade ~$0.10) × the number of dev tasks.\nA full dev gate is ~30 tasks ≈ ~$33. **Metered** — charged per task up to the remaining cap; tasks\nbeyond the cap come back as `skipped_for_budget`. The gate is your **highest-value spend** (it is the\nonly held-out generalization signal), so budget for it: score only your **top 1–2** train-picked\ncandidates (CLAUDE.md §4), but score each on a **large** dev batch — the **full set is best**; a small\nsubset is a noisy read that overfits. Reserve enough cap to run at least **one full gate** as your\ncommit decision (and ideally a second, to re-gate after fixing a thrash). Reserve enough **wall-clock**\ntoo — a full gate runs ~90 min, and `dev_eval` **refuses to start a full gate that can't finish","is_error":false}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4283aaf1-9e61-4711-af01-0dc2c98501ec","uuid":"02a96a6a-34ca-40ea-95d4-7b319d9f5350","timestamp":"2026-06-28T20:38:37.449Z","tool_use_result":{"stdout":"=== any saved dev per-task data? ===\nscratch/:\ntotal 48\ndrwxrwxr-x 3 ubuntu ubuntu  4096 Jun 28 20:35 .\ndrwx------ 6 ubuntu ubuntu  4096 Jun 28 20:29 ..\n-rw-rw-r-- 1 ubuntu ubuntu     0 Jun 28 20:29 .gitkeep\n-rw-r--r-- 1 ubuntu ubuntu  5105 Jun 28 17:45 NOTES.md\n-rw-r--r-- 1 root   root   21155 Jun 28 20:35 agent_loop.iter2.bak\n-rw-r--r-- 1 root   root    1870 Jun 28 20:32 dup_analysis.py\ndrwxr-xr-x 3 ubuntu ubuntu  4096 Jun 28 16:30 test\n\nscratch/test/:\ntotal 20\ndrwxr-xr-x 3 ubuntu ubuntu 4096 Jun 28 16:30 .\ndrwxrwxr-x 3 ubuntu ubuntu 4096 Jun 28 20:35 ..\ndrwxr-xr-x 3 ubuntu ubuntu 4096 Jun 28 14:41 harness\n-rw-r--r-- 1 ubuntu ubuntu 2866 Jun 28 14:41 t.py\n-rw-r--r-- 1 ubuntu ubuntu 1474 Jun 28 16:30 t2.py\n/workspace/.claude/tools/dev_eval.md\n/workspace/.claude/tools/dev_eval\n=== trend.json structure ===\n<class 'dict'>\n['latest_iter', 'n_tasks', 'iters', 'train_mean_by_iter', 'baseline_iter', 'trend', 'improved_vs_prev', 'harmed_vs_prev', 'improved_vs_bare', 'harmed_vs_bare']\n=== dev_eval.md (how it reports + baseline) ===\n# Tool — `dev_eval`\n\n> Your **commit gate**: score your current `harness/` on the held-out-from-train **DEV set**, graded\n> by the **ensemble** judge — the same grader the canonical verdict uses.\n\n## Purpose\n\n`dev_eval` runs the frozen Harvey agent on each **DEV** task using your **current `harness/`**, then\ngrades each deliverable with the **ensemble judge** (gpt-5-mini + gpt-5, escalating disagreements to\nSonnet). This per-doc bound holds regardless of the global limit below.\n#   • SECONDARY backstop is this GLOBAL limit: after this many *distinct* re-fetch\n#     events across the whole run, eviction is disabled entirely (reverting to bare\n#     for the rest of the run). It guards the pathological \"re-read EVERYTHING\"\n#     flail (a many-small-docs extraction task that, once disrupted, re-reads all\n#     its inputs) before it can re-inflate context.\n# Why 4 (raised from 1): limit=1 disabled eviction on a redline's FIRST backward\n# reference, so the cost-dominant redline GIANTS (subsequent/first-turn redlines,\n# 13-15M input each) reverted to bare and captured ~no savings — the bulk of the\n# remaining cost.
